--- Commit Message ---
LU-8130 ldlm: convert ldlm_resource hash to rhashtable

Using an rhashtable allows lockless lookup at the cost
of rcu freeing of entries.

When we find an entry, we need to atomically check the
reference hasn't dropped to zero.

When adding an entry, we might find an existing entry which is in the
process of being removed - with a zero refcount.  In that case
we loop around and repeat the lookup.  To ensure this doesn't
spin, the 'cmp' function will fail any comparison with a resource
which has a zero refcount.

Now that we are using resizing hash tables, we don't need to preconfig
suitable sizes for each namespace.  We can just use the default and
let it grow or shrink as needed.  We keep the pre-configured sizes
for the bucket array.  Previously the sizeof the bucket array was the
difference between nsd_all_bits and nsd_bkt_bits.  As we don't need
nsd_all_bits any more, nsd_bkt_bits is changed to the number of bits
used to choose a bucket.

Walking an rhashtable requires that we manage refcounts ourself, so
a new function, ldlm_resource_for_each() is added to do that.
Note that with this patch we now update a per-table counter
on every insert/remove, which might cause more contention
between CPUs on a busy system.  Hopefully rhashtable will
be enhanced in the new future to support a per-CPU counter
for nelems.

Only use call_rcu() to free slab resources that have been removed
from the rhashtable, other cases can be free immediately.

Signed-off-by: NeilBrown <neil@brown.name>
Signed-off-by: Shaun Tancheff <shaun.tancheff@hpe.com>
Signed-off-by: James Simmons <jsimmons@infradead.org>

--- Message (Neil Brown, 2022-12-09 03:54:55.000000000) ---
Patch Set 5:

> Patch Set 5:
> 
> [ 1299.954141] LDISKFS-fs (dm-6): mounted filesystem with ordered data mode. Opts: user_xattr,errors=remount-ro,no_mbcache,nodelalloc
> [ 1300.270900] BUG: unable to handle kernel NULL pointer dereference at 0000000000000038
> [ 1300.272402] PGD 80000000341cf067 P4D 80000000341cf067 PUD 341ce067 PMD 0 
> [ 1300.273632] Oops: 0000 [#1] SMP PTI
> [ 1300.274344] CPU: 0 PID: 81418 Comm: mount.lustre Kdump: loaded Tainted: G           OE    --------- -  - 4.18.0-372.32.1.el8_lustre.x86_64 #1
> [ 1300.276552] Hardware name: Red Hat KVM, BIOS 0.5.1 01/01/2011
> [ 1300.277588] RIP: 0010:rs_cmp+0x9/0x50 [ptlrpc]
> [ 1300.278908] Code: fd 64 a1 da 66 66 2e 0f 1f 84 00 00 00 00 00 66 90 66 66 66 66 90 48 83 c7 60 e9 c2 97 f5 d9 66 90 66 66 66 66 90 48 8b 47 08 <48> 8b 4e 40 48 39 08 74 0a b8 fd ff ff ff e9 c4 64 a1 da 48 8b 4e

This tells me that the failing code is :
   0:	66 66 66 66 90       	data16 data16 data16 xchg %ax,%ax
   5:	48 8b 47 08          	mov    0x8(%rdi),%rax
   9:*	48 8b 4e 40          	mov    0x40(%rsi),%rcx		<-- trapping instruction
   d:	48 39 08             	cmp    %rcx,(%rax)

rdi is arg, rsi is obj which is 0xfffffffffffffff8

obj_cmpfn is always called "params.obj_cmpfn(&arg, rht_obj(ht, he))" and as head_offset is 8, that means "he" must have been NULL.

That should be impossible, but could happen if the rhash_head was corrupted....

Which probably happens when call_rcu is called while some other thread is looking at that res.

So we cannot union lr_rcu with lr_hash.

It should be ask to union lr_rcu with lr_lock or lr_waiting or anything except lr_head, lr_refcount, lr_name as they are the only bit that a lookup might touch before successfully getting a reference.

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2023-12-05 20:41:23.000000000) ---
Patch Set 10:

So the purpose of this patch is basically to move to shared code and eventually remove the libcfs hash table, right?  We have no particular reason to think this improves performance *in this instance*?  Just trying to make sure I understand the situation and working theory here.  I haven't seen the resource hash be a problem in the past, but I'm in favor of cleanup/moving to shared code.

--- Message (Timothy Day, 2023-12-06 02:33:04.000000000) ---
Patch Set 10:

(3 comments)

This patch seems to replace some spinlocks with rcu locking. I think that'd lead to less lock contention in ldlm_resource_get() and other places?

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2023-12-06 03:07:14.000000000) ---
Patch Set 10:

Right, I understand the theory, but I've never seen that to be costly or contended.  It might be there's a small benefit in, eg, a single file/stripe DIO IOPs workload on the server side.

Like I said, I'm fine with this even if it's performance neutral, I'm mostly curious.

--- Message (Neil Brown, 2023-12-06 07:51:56.000000000) ---
Patch Set 10:

> Patch Set 10:
> 
> So the purpose of this patch is basically to move to shared code and eventually remove the libcfs hash table, right? 

That is my understanding - yes.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2023-12-06 08:23:14.000000000) ---
Patch Set 10:

In theory there is a lookup problem as a client gets to 100k cached locks or more, per LU-16365. It was my hope that changing to rhashtable would improve that workload, but there is no confirmation of this. 

The reason this isn't landed yet is that it breaks el7 clients, which are still at least in some  use.  I have no objection to removing el7.9 server support from master, but client support is more widely used.  

I'm not sure how easy it would be to make the ldlm cutover to rhashtable a build-time decision based on the kernel version. That would be phased out when el7.9 clients stop being used, but would defer the final cleanup of the hashtable code.

--- Message (James Simmons, 2023-12-12 19:53:47.000000000) ---
Patch Set 10:

> Patch Set 10:
> 
> (3 comments)
> 
> This patch seems to replace some spinlocks with rcu locking. I think that'd lead to less lock contention in ldlm_resource_get() and other places?

In theory yes. Numbers need to be collected.

>  > What do you expect to gain from that?  I can't see the point
>  > myself, but maybe there is one.
> 
> As with the interval tree code, it is good to measure the performance impact or improvement of this change to the core code.


Ahh.. For some reason I thought you were suggesting some extra testing for the interval tree code, but you aren't.  You are suggesting a completely different test to exercise the resource lookup code.

While I agree that would be a good idea in general, I think the design improvements of the rhashtable code over the cfs_hash code are so obvious that any performance impact would be extremely surprising.
With extent trees we aren't really testing the extent-tree code, but rather testing the impact of changing the optimization for lots of identical extents.  There is no similar special casing with lookup (is there?) so no likelihood of interesting results.

So I wouldn't find that adding of a test to be worth the effort.  If someone else does, I'll happily review it.

Patch Set 31:

Normally I would reject this mass of #ifdefs, but in this case I totally understand the motivation for this and agree it is a short term ugliness in order to move forward for newer kernels.

My one suggestion would be that instead of using "#if LINUX_KERNEL_VERSION" for all the checks that this instead be changed to "#ifdef USE_RHEL79_LDLM_RESOURCE_HASH" or similar, and set that in  e.g. lustre_dlm.h, so that this is easier to find in the code and remove in the future.

I know it won't be this way for a long time, but who knows when someone will have time to remove this code (which will hopefully soon be dead), and people forget or get distracted with other tasks.  This will make it pretty clear why all these conditionals exist.

I'm not dead set on this (hopefully we will also be doing other el7.9 cleanups when it is removed), but just an idea to make this cleaner.
